<Name>Summer Sandberg<//Name><date>1621920059466< /date><Rating>5<//Rating>< review>
Me and a foodie friend hit this place up on a Friday night. We Make it a habit to try new restaurants pretty often and this place was delicious. It was our first time here, and our server made some absolutely spot-on recommendations. Every single item we got was delicious.
We had the waygu fat washed type of old-fashioned, 'the last melon' which was a gin drink, and then the chai paloma. All were very unique and delicious. Well balanced.
We continued with the hamachi which was exceptional, the citrus salad that was light and fresh with perfect flavors, and the spicy fried rice that blue our minds. I believe there are two fried rice types on the menu but it was the newer one that was super spicy that was absolutely incredible. We also had the seared bluefin tuna which was done perfectly as well. We finished with these beignets type-filled donuts and I can't remember the name. I wasn't expecting them to be as incredible as they were, lol. We also got the matcha layered type of mousse cake.  Compared to those stuffed donuts, the matcha dessert was a little bland but still good.
All in all we were extremely pleased and impressed by the items we chose and what our waiter recommended.
The absolute only downside of the menu is that a Good portion of it offers fried food.  At this price point, It was a little surprising.  We still can't wait to go back and try some of the other items!<//review>

<text>Delicious food! Got to meet famous Chef Brian Malarkey.<//text><Pictures>None</Pictures><response>None< /response>< gmap_id>
0x80d9559fafe293b7:0xe74b70321582b549</gmap_id>
</record></dataset><record>
<review>This was an all-around amazing experience! From the front of the house to the back of the house, this place deserves every one of my 5 stars.

I chose this place to celebrate my 33rd birthday because I was intrigued by the elevated Asian-fusion concept.  This is Top Chef's Brian Malarkey's newest restaurant that opened just a year ago, and I was so excited to try it!  Like another reviewer on here said before, the indoor decor is very Crazy Rich Asians meets Mad Men/Great Gatsby kind of feel.  You automatically feel sophisticated upon walking in.

There is plenty of parking on the street if you come here these days during COVID and on a weeknight like we did last night.  Otherwise, there is a clearly marked valet right out front.

Service:
The entire front of the house staff worked like a team and was well-coordinated in their timing of clearing dishes, cleaning up after every course, and refilling the water.  I never once felt forgotten about.
Our server was Drew, who was amazing!  He was very personable and did a great job at explaining the food and the night's special, and answering all of our questions about anything.

On to the food:

COCKTAILS
We started the evening ordering the Cherry Blossom Margarita and Thai Tai, which was a rum with Thai tea drink.  The Thai tai was visually stunning with powdered ube on top!  The cherry blossom margarita was also very tasty (so tasty, I ordered a second one halfway through our meal).

HAMACHI WITH ASIAN PEAR
This was one of our appetizers from the cold section.  The fish was perfectly seasoned, and I enjoyed the kimchi vinaigrette and watermelon radish to give it texture.  I would definitely order this again, as the flavors came together naturally and it all just worked.

COCONUT SHRIMP KARAAGE
This was a hot appetizer dish, and it was shrimp with a panko bread (I think) breading with coconut flakes.  The surprise of this dish was how well the green curry mayo dipping sauce was constructed!  I could eat that all day with anything

ANIMAE BUNS
A must try, and this is probably their signature dish for appetizers.  They were four golf-ball sized buns with a generous dressing of miso seaweed butter that was sweet and topped with sesame seeds.  I would have ordered more if I had the room for it!

JAPANESE A5 SATSUMA STRIP
I was very excited to see A5 wagyu beef on the menu, so naturally I had to try it.  At $22/oz it's definitely a luxury, but worth it for a birthday dinner splurge.  The beef is triple seared in a salt crust, sake, and finished the soy sauce as the final step.  The way the meat is treated really shines through in the flavor

THAI EGG NOODLE & JIDORI CHICKEN
This was one of my husband's plate entrees he ordered.  He personally isn't a fan of the standard thin noodles, preferring a thicker noodle.  But other than that, he said the chicken was well seasoned with a nice balance of the flavors in the sauce

WAGYU BURGER
This was my husband's second plate entree.  It is not served on a burger bun - instead, it's on a thick piece of toasted milk bread.  He said it was a little too thick in proportion for the burger, but the flavors were on point again.

COMPLIMENTARY "RICE" ICE CREAM
This was a nice finish to the evening.  It came with a birthday candle and the bottom was a tasty chewy cookie/brownie feel.  Next time we come here I definitely want to try the Vietnamese iced coffee with bad donuts.  At this point we were both too full to order that.

We left with full stomachs and smiling faces.  Cheers, Animae!  100% recommended to anyone I know.< /review><time>1612458757170< /time>< rate>
5</rate>

<review>I went here recently and had a great experience. I've been walking by the construction of this restaurant for so long, I did not expect the final result to live up to the suspense, but it definitely did. Upon entering, I was immediately blown away by the decor and ambiance. I'll be back just to sit at the bar and take it all in for sure.

The food managed to be as good as the interior, and we loved all of our dishes. If you're looking for a beautiful place to visit now that indoor seating is back, don't miss this one

A side note: I was lucky enough to sit inside, but the outdoor seating looked extremely lacking. I have to say my review might be very different if I had to sit on the side of the busy street. They might consider constructing some sort of enclosed area like so many restaurants in the gaslamp, although I know their location might make than untenable. I know this is something out of their control, and obviously they were not planning for this situation, but if you are going to make a reservation make sure you give yourself enough time to get a table inside - it's worth waiting a bit longer.< /review><date>1602006001950< /date></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Disappointed.

The location and the indoor decor is nice.
The service was ok, nothing bad or exceptional, but as someone who dine alone I‚Äôd like to find back my table not completely cleaned when I come back from the bathroom...

I started with the toro tartare. The fish was good and the presentation looked refined. Good point here.

The disappointment started after my order of ~7 oz of A5 wagyu came to my table. No problem with the meat. It‚Äôs standard A5, well cooked and just enough salty like I liked.
Good for you because my waiter didn‚Äôt bothered asking me how I would like the meat cooked. What if I was a fan of rare or well done wagyu?

According to the menu the meat is supposed to be served with ¬´¬†a selection if sauces and banchan¬†¬ª. I didn‚Äôt see any of that on my table. Just the meat and some kind of fishy tasting salt on the side. No explanation given on what it was.

At $130 for the meat only, adding a little side of rice, lettuce, whatever, ... would be much more appreciated.

Now for the dessert I ordered the crispy charcoal toast. First bite let me thought I would end with a positive note. Second bite disgusted me. There is an interesting taste overall completely RUINED by the saltiness. There is too much miso butter which turns the whole dessert into something over salty which is sad because overall it could be excellent without that mistake.

Bill came at $197$ with a diet coke, a bottle of sparkling water and a mysterious fee of 4%, wtf?

I will not recommend AT ALL.</review>

<user_id>112365912157377424550<//user_id><Name>Gene ≈Åee</Name><Time>1583648067409</Time>< rating>
5<//rating>
< Review>
Last night, we went to the much-acclaimed restaurant called Animae, which is the new venture by the Puffer Malarkey Collective. Brian Malarkey is known for his restaurants, such as Searsucker, Herringbone, and Gingham.

We were there to celebrate our 4 year anniversary (yes, again!); this place was a special treat for ourselves. Definitely make reservations, though there is a bar in the front area, with the picture of a robot floating in the ocean with koi.

The restaurant is on the ground floor in the ultra high-end condominiums Pacific Gate by Bosa, which we think formerly was the SDG&E headquarters. We loved the transformation of the area, with the beautiful Intercontinental hotel next door. Parking in that area can be tough but we got there around 6pm, which is probably still early before the dinner crowd.

Once you walk in, you can see the plush decor, with the bronze olive colored drapes. Right off the bat, we were greeted with smiles and immediately seated at our table, with spectacular service by our waitress Emily, who asked if we wanted champagne, with a wink suggesting she knew we were there for our anniversary. I did note it in the reservation, so it impressed me that she was mindful of it. The staff refilled our water without asking. There's a giant piece of charcoal in the water pitcher, supposedly filtering it, but I'm not sure how much of that works or is for show.

We ordered two drinks, the Sukiyaki Western, which was whisky with passion fruit and ginger, which was delicious. Mike had Thai Tai, which tasted like a creamsicle and was slightly disappointing.

We started with three appetizers, including their butter dumplings, corn elote, and Tom Yum mushrooms. The butter dumplings were definitely very different than typical xiaolongbao, in that they have a lot of butter and the filling is escargot, and was quite delicious. It is served on a bed of wagyu capaccio, which I would recommend that one. Mike thought the corn elote was okay, but he enjoyed the mushroom appetizer more, which I thought that was somewhat too salty. Emily did bring all over a bowl of rice to help mellow the saltiness.

We chose two entrees: the cod, and the pork belly and egg noodles - both were good and I would recommend.

Our friend Michael also recommended the Korean Fried Chicken, but we did not try that one.

For our final part of the meal, we had dessert. We couldn't decide between the Pavlova and the malasadas, so Emily accommodated us with a flight of both! The malasada is a cinnamon donut with coconut cream, served on pureed passion fruit, and topped with Thai green curry ice cream. They were both good, but I would say the malasadas was outstanding. I would go back alone for the malasadas!

Along with the dessert, Emily brought us 2 glasses of champagne, and again congratulated us on our anniversary.

From start to end, we had a fantastic time, though the noise level was higher than expected, especially given the amount of soft decor to absorb the sound. Not sure if I would say every dish was spectacular, but it was definitely a different take on Asian fusion cuisine, and I did not hate the Wagyu. Also, the prices are not unreasonable, and this is a place where I would take out of town guests as well as friends and family for special occasions.< /Review>

<text>Dinner was incredible! The ingenuity of the food, the impeccable attention-to-detail across every touchpoint, and the interplay of texture envelopes you. It's almost like the entire experience is a play on the Yin & Yang - the food is East meets West in a way that awakens the palette and expands your culinary horizons, the ambiance is old-world elegance meets modern design. It's all so tonal and creatively balanced, and truly like nothing I've seen before. Our server Drew was also fantastic, and everyone we interacted with was so knowledgeable and professional, yet warm.

If you're a foodie, I highly recommend trying Animae!< /text>< pictures>

<name>Spickle exe< /name><date>1570518182844< /date><Rate>5</Rate>< review>
Redefining fine dining. Dare I say it? Hell yes.

The Animae experience is akin to immersing yourself in a plush, velvet cocoon and emerging to an exquisitely reimagined, soul-satiating, visual-auditory-dining experience. With a not-so-apologetic nod to the 70‚Äôs, a cheeky penchant for vintage robots and exquisite taste in wall coverings, Chris Puffer‚Äôs never-ending quest for the ultimate ambiance does not disappoint; this time proving to be the zenith of platters from which to savor chef Brian Malarkey‚Äôs futuristic spins on Asian- fusion cuisine.

I literally fall asleep thinking about the Tom-Yum Mushrooms with Burrata, and the Old Fashioned has no local rivals that I‚Äôm aware of. Not to mention the staff at every Puffer Malarkey Collective establishment is the creme de la creme. Do yourself a favor and drop in. You‚Äôre welcome.</review>

<user>114446462602619042239< /user><GmapID>0x80d9559fafe293b7:0xe74b70321582b549< /GmapID><Rating>4<//Rating><Pics>None</Pics><Time>1571252206587<//Time></record></dataset><record>
<Rate>1</Rate><Review>Open Table wouldn't record my review.

Here we go:

I'm so sad to say this is no Herb & Wood experience Mr Malarkey. We have eaten at several of your restaurants over the past few years for special occasions and once again we expected to have a fantastic time here for my wife's birthday NOPE.  9 pm reservation confirmed twice and didn't get seated until 9:30 pm. Waited at the bar for 10 minutes for a drink that came with a bit of attitude. Remember we are here for the food and to experience the beautifully detailed restaurant.
Menu Choice:
Coal Fired Octopus Skewer: Interior texture was good but we couldn't get past the burnt taste I mean burnt like burnt to a cinder.

Hirasama: Who puts Cocoa nibs with raw fish and compliments it with a sweet drizzle. I thought my palate was lying to me.

Chili Garlic Lobster: I counted 10 strands of noodles ( You can tell i'm sad now on a Saturday night) Lobster pieces perfect amount YES. Hold ON why is the bisque burning the back of my throat guess what?? someone dropped the salt shaker in the sauce and forgot to taste test.

All said and done here comes the Birthday Cake / slice: Presentation perfect but can we all agree that cake especially birthday cake even cheese cake is sweet. This was bitter even after removing the coulis (Sauce)  on a base of cinder block. My mouth has left the building and spat out my tong on the way.

Why didn't we speak up??
Young couple next to us out on a date leaving 3 kids at home under the age of 3 DATE NIGHT. So the last thing I would want would be people complaining about food and spoiling my night off.

Animae I do not spend time writing reviews unless It really burns a hole in my head good or bad 2 days later.

Jason G.<//Review>< Gmap_id>

< text>
Just finished dinner and wondering what we actually ate?? Snow pea salad tasted like fish and was super salty. The dumpling and carpaccio dish was the best thing we had.

Mushrooms that the waiter raved about were mediocre at best.

Sweet breads were too salty and chewy.

Honestly,  we will not return. I never leave reviews on restaurants but was truly disappointed at the prices, portions and food quality/taste. The waiter seemed so excited and was very animated when discussing dish selections so we went with his recommendations and tried several different items.

The best thing on the menu is the over priced wine. I‚Äôve loved all the other sister restaurants and was so excited to try Animae. They just got a little too weird with the food.< /text>

< text>
Tried out this restaurant for the first time last night. Decor was stunning, booths were beautiful and ambiance was chic. We ordered appetizers and most were great-mushrooms, sweet potato and corn. All had their delicious flavor. Cucumber salad was delicious and refreshing.

Entrees came and the snapper was a crowd pleaser. Both the Kung pao chicken and the stir fry vegetables were drenched in this overwhelming salty and strong sauce, taking all the crunch out of the veggies. Needless to say we didn‚Äôt eat much of it.

Desserts were a huge disappointment. One was some sort of charcoal chocolate cake with pieces of flavorless cardboard type to ‚Äúdecorate‚Äù it. Another was a slush that was basically ice with some jam...not impressive. Another was some sort of donut bites that smelled so greasy, like they were fried in old oil. Oh, and our teas arrived lukewarm as well.

Sometimes when you try too hard to be different, it doesn‚Äôt work. In this case it worked for some items like the apps, but not all the entrees and definitely not the dessert.<//text>

< review>
Animae was as delightful and unique dinning experience as I have had and I am a long time San Diegan.  From the d√©cor of art deco and modern animation design to the staff who were willing participants in providing you the ‚Äúdiner‚Äù a clear understanding of the restaurant‚Äôs concept and menu.  To the menu, which as I had followed Chef Joe (who I loved at Cucina Urbana where he was the executive chef) in his travels earlier in the year up north where he was tasting and building this menu into a one that offers a unique and flavorful selection.  All the staff were on board and there when needed without exception.  I had an early reservation and having the privilege having owned fine dinning establishments in NYC and LA I witnessed something I rarely if ever see in San Diego. One of the serving staff was measuring a table to ensure the proper placement of all the settings.  To me that was of particular delight as it shows the commitment is universal and held to a high standard to make the diner‚Äôs evening a memorable experience whether you are in for just the tasting menu or the full approach. The wine list and sake‚Äô selection was great, but I did not partake this time next I will.   Kudos to the staff, Chef Joe and of course its purveyor Brian Malarkey.  This should set a standard for others if they wish to be in this arena. As for myself I am looking forward to returning soon.</review>

< Review>
Flew to Tahoe to enjoy trails and snow play with friends. This nonprofit is well run and volunteers/staff so friendly! Reminded us of Shasta Nordic--we so appreciate their service sharing their love of the outdoors.
We went on 4.3.21, the last day open for Nordic skiing. A few dirt patches to walk past but well groomed, beautiful trails and such friendly visitors. Dropped my Visa CC on the trail and picked it up at lost and found. So grateful for the fun day in beautiful nature and restored faith in humanity.</Review>

<rating>5</rating><UserId.>116688653851063668748<//UserId.>< review>
Best Day! I am a complete novice. The staff was so helpful. They answered my questions  ahead of time when I phoned (What kind of shoes to wear? Rentals include shoes); greeted me warmly when I arrived; patiently explained rental and lesson options; gave me a few cross country tips; provided clear map routes; rental equipment was in great shape; trails were clearly marked and perfectly groomed. The weather was beyond perfect and plenty of snow on the ground. Benches and warming huts scattered throughout the various courses. No dog poop anywhere even though there are designated dog times. The facility has a small, limited breakfast/lunch menu which includes fresh baked cookies. My cousin and I had just the very best experience!  Both of us have injured knees due to downhill skiing. Both of us have received recommendations from our orthopedic surgeons to try cross country. And both of us had a blast without further tweaking our grumpy knees. JUST DO IT!</review>

The trails are groomed nightly by highly skilled snowcat operators who are passionate about their work. Daily trail passes and season pass sales don't recover all the costs associated with grooming and operations. Donations are encouraged to our non-profit (501c3) Tahoe Cross Country Ski Education Association, whose mission is to provide free and affordable programs and trail access for local kids and families."}<//response>

<Text>I've driven by Yalla Yalla a few times and hadn't had a chance to stop by so tonight I had dinner with some friends and we all loved it! We were so full but we wanted to keep eating! This is great for takeout as there isn't much seating. <Rating>5<//Rating><review>I love a good 'hole-in-the-wall' mom and pop shop. The building may not be 'fancy' but you know you're gonna get some legit authentic food. I tried the chicken shawarma and date cookie. The chicken was well seasoned and juicy. I was pleasantly surprised to find it stuffed with cabbage rather than lettuce, which makes sense since lettuce gets soggy in a hot shawarma. I think the cabbage made it more hearty (plus I love cabbage). The date cookie is soft and lightly sweet (should have had it with tea or coffee). Food was so good, I ended ordering a beef kabob plate togo for my hubby to try. Will definitely eat here again.</review></record>

<review>Recently had a flat due to a screw puncturing the tire and took the vehicle here because it was convenient (close proximity to home and late evening hours).  The counter staff was nice enough and tended to us without any appointments quickly.

The shop was unable to patch the tire because the puncture was too far down on the sidewall so the staff suggested getting a set of replacement tires for the drive wheels - no issue with that.  The shop had a set of two decent Goodyear tires in stock and was able to install them within an hour.

The tires sold to us are no longer made by Goodyear or sold by any other tire dealers that we could find.  This seems to explain the date on the tires indicating they were made in 2012.  It seemed that these tires were mostly sold by walmart.  These were likely bought cheap and resold by the shop at a 20-30% markup.

The major issues came the next day driving to work and the low tire pressure indicator came on.  When I stopped to check my tires I found that the two new ones were at 50psi (which was the max for the tire) and the 2 original tires were both 10psi under the manuf requirements.

The lack of attention to detail is a huge disappointment for the shop.  I like to go to local businesses but I do not have the patience or time to deal with incompetence.  When you can not properly do the main thing your business is designed to do - perhaps it is time to analyze your business practices.

Perhaps this is a one time case of improper training, however I will not recommend or return to this place for any service.</review>< pictures>
None</pictures>

Starbucks over all customer service is generally acceptable.
Sometimes lacking the genuine enthusiasm that should come from a greeting.
The problem that I sometimes have is with the new employees being trained.
The new trainings are not always up on how to mix a drink.
I suggested that they give a reminder that if they're not 100% sure that they should take a look at the recipe.
This in itself would be a huge improvement and I wouldn't have to put out the time effort and energy to call and make an additional stop to Starbucks just to correct what they should have already done in the 1st place.
I mention all of this because this has happened more times than I would like to count, not only by me but my daughter who is a regular at Starbucks as well. We order the same thing and have the same problem getting customer service to get it right the first time.......coffee/tea anyone?<//Review>
